  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e2e9a6e-10ef-48b7-8f62-b747e2d4e86a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

And with time running out, and mistakes catching up with them, Sophie and her allies must join forces in ways they never have before.</span>

    <a title="Mossring" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36697449-mossring"><img alt="Mossring" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490456347p2/36697449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795410993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6995743063859588756"><blockquote><i>They weren't friends. And they weren't </i>actually<i> sisters.<br/>They were just two different girls from two different worlds.</i></blockquote><br/>There are a lot of things I can say about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_' title='Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nightfall</a>, but one thing I'm 100% sure of is that it was way better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___5_' title='Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #5) by Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lodestar</a>. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_' title='Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nightfall</a> picks up right after the last scene of the previous book, where Sophie meets her adoptive younger sister, Amy, and talks to her for the first time since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_' title='Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Keeper of the Lost Cities</a>, when Sophie leaves her adoptive family and sets off for a completely</span>
  <span id="freeText6995743063859588756" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>They weren't friends. And they weren't </i>actually<i> sisters.<br />They were just two different girls from two different worlds.</i></blockquote><br />There are a lot of things I can say about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_" title="Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfall</a>, but one thing I'm 100% sure of is that it was way better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_" title="Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfall</a> picks up right after the last scene of the previous book, where Sophie meets her adoptive younger sister, Amy, and talks to her for the first time since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a>, when Sophie leaves her adoptive family and sets off for a completely new life in the Lost Cities. I really liked how Shannon handled the whole situation about Amy, and I really like the relationship between Sophie and Amy in this book. It was nice to see an outside perspective of the Lost Cities from Amy and it felt sort of like a parallel with Book 1 when Sophie finds out about the Lost Cities for the first time. I also enjoyed how well written Sophie's thoughts about Amy were, and how conflicted she felt.<br /><br /><blockquote>Three <i>hands. No fourth for her. It was how it should be. How it would</i> have<i> to be. And Sophie could live with that. She could let them go again, to spare them that pain. But it would still hurt. It would </i>always<i> hurt.</i></blockquote><br />The only complaint I have about Amy is that I felt that she could have played a bigger role in the book. She spends most of the book cooped up in her house in the Lost Cities, and while I understood that it was to keep her safe, I couldn't help wishing she could do more. <br /><br />I enjoyed the plot in this book better than the previous book. The concept of Nightfall was alright, at most a little underwhelming, but it was still good. I loved the main climax of the book, which is the scene on the cover <s>because my daughter Linh was actually doing something important for once</s>. There were some new characters, such as the escaped prisoner in Lumeneria, whom I liked because she was an interesting villain to read about, and she was a fresh breeze after all the things we've read about Fintan, Brant, Gethen, Alvar, Lady Gisela and Ruy. <br /><br />Also, I loved loved loved the part where Choralmere was featured—it's so pretty and I would love to live there. There was some extra insight into the Song family and the story behind their surname, which I appreciated very much. <s>Not to mention how Tam kept burning Quan and Mai.</s><br /><br />There were some plot twists that I called<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (I'd called Marella being a Pyrokinetic since 2015) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I had been planning to put <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ruy breaking the force field in Atlantis <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in my own story, but Shannon wrote it down before I could and if I write it in now, everyone would think I'm Unoriginal™ so I'm probably never going to finish that fic now. But that aside, I really liked what went down in the book. There was a lot of action and suspense that kept me turning the pages. (Or at least, tapping the side of my Kindle screen.)<br /><br />With the introduction of Amy, I found Sophie's character to be more developed in this book, and I liked how ready she was to sacrifice something important to protect the people she loved, even if it meant giving in to the enemy. Fitz... was okay, if you counted how supportive and sweet he was towards Sophie—I really liked that—but I would wish to see more from him. Biana was really brave in this book, and she went all the way to defend and protect her friends and family. That, I'm proud of. I loved Dex in this book, as usual, but in this book, he became even braver and smarter. I really liked how Shannon wrote him in this book and I hope to see more in Book 7 <s>where I hope he would actually be on the cover for once</s>. Keefe was much more enjoyable to read about compared to Book 5, where I found him quite annoying. He is brave and reckless and loyal and I can't wait to read more about him. <br /><br />And needless to say, I loved Tam and Linh. I didn't know it was possible to love Tam even more, but now I know. I think Linh is the wisest out of the eight, and I really liked the dynamic in this book where she changed from a person who is afraid of the water, who cannot control the water, to a person who bonds with the water and is in complete control of the water. Though she didn't appear as much as I wanted her to, as most of the book she was in the background hanging out with Wylie. And I don't like her with Wylie. I don't ship her with anyone, actually. Speaking of Wylie, I wished he would play a bigger role in the book. I didn't really like Marella in this book as her personality is kind of annoying, but I suppose that's to be expected, considering what had happened to her. I think she'll grow onto me again soon though!<br /><br />I don't really talk about shipping because it's subjective, but this book made me ship Sokeefe. I didn't really like them in Book 5. I thought the short story in the Barnes and Noble limited edition was really sweet, how Keefe had feelings for Sophie but chose not to act on them because he knew Sophie wasn't ready and might not like it. Also, I ship Tam and Biana, but there were little to no scenes in the book, which was kind of disappointing. I was also looking out for LGBT+ scenes. I hope there's more in the next book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I screamed when Sophie and Dex kissed (I'd lowkey shipped them as they're kind of cute together), and was a tad disappointed when Shannon killed the ship (I mean <i>why did you have to make Dex sad, it was heartwrenching to see him avoiding Sophie</i>) but I admire the way Shannon handled it, she handled it excellently and left me feeling sad but satisfied. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The ending of the book was a cliffhanger (like always), but it's an overused plot device in many books, so it felt a little lackluster compared to the ending of Book 5. Nevertheless, I still look forward to what happens in Book 7! All in all, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_" title="Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfall</a> was a very enjoyable read and it definitely deserves the five stars... or should I say six, since it's Book 6? That was a bad joke, so I'll leave now and Vanish off the face of the earth until Book 7 comes out. When that happens, I'll suddenly appear <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like how Forkman appeared after supposedly being stabbed to death by Gethen <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6995743063859588756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15539458113511760498">*sigh* Counting the days until I can read this. <br/><b>Countdown: </b>Approximately, 3 months and 30 more days to go!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478447558ra/21073467.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*finally finishes the very last page after seven months later*<br/><br/>Okay, um, that was... interesting. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531061071ra/25941874.gif' width='360' height='360' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Did anyone else feel like this was being rushed? Like Mrs. Messenger was trying to write Nightfall as quickly as possible so that her dear readers would have some new installment by November? The reason why I ask this is because throughout the book, it felt like everything was going by too fast o</span>
  <span id="freeText15539458113511760498" style="display:none">*sigh* Counting the days until I can read this. <br><b>Countdown: </b>Approximately, 3 months and 30 more days to go!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478447558ra/21073467.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*finally finishes the very last page after seven months later*<br><br>Okay, um, that was... interesting. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531061071ra/25941874.gif" width="360" height="360" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Did anyone else feel like this was being rushed? Like Mrs. Messenger was trying to write Nightfall as quickly as possible so that her dear readers would have some new installment by November? The reason why I ask this is because throughout the book, it felt like everything was going by too fast or I just wasn’t able to be up to speed with everything. And the missions they carried out? Yeah. Not my cup of tea, unfortunately. Why some KOTLC fans will say that this is the greatest book of THE ENTIRE SERIES, I will never understand. And here’s something from you: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I feel that the story would’ve been a lot more interesting if Forkle actually did die. Yes, I said it. Through the first five books, Forkle was GREAT, but when his supposed twin brother took his slot, the story just continued on as usual. Nothing daring and exciting really happened, unless you count the fact that Keefe got injured by the troll king. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’m sorry, but Nightfall isn’t the greatest book of the series! It was bland through half of the book, and it kept recycling the story from previous books. And to add on to my rant, I was so sad to see that Dex was hardly mentioned. Sure, he had things to do with the Black Swan but... I was disappointed to see that the little muffin didn’t get as much... spotlight? than everyone else. He received as much mentioned as Wylie, and that’s not a whole lot. Now that we’re going further into the series, you would expect to see changes with Sophie. Is she as bland as the previous books? Yes. Does she always believe she can do things by herself and is always easily persuaded with the help of her friends? Yes. See? NOTHING HAS CHANGED WITH SOPHIE!!! She hasn’t PROGRESSED, and grown since the very beginning! I guess that was the most infuriating part about this. Sophie didn’t seem to mature. I guarantee you. If you read Nightfall again (I know, how horrible of me to say) and read the first book, you will see NO change with Sophie from when she was twelve to however old she is now. She’s not eighteen or sixteen, is she? I’m sorry, but the timeline is also super confusing. Yes, Mrs. Messenger DOES mention everyone’s height and whatnot, but you never get a clear picture of how OLD they are. And what should they look like now that they are OLDER and MATURE. If it wasn’t for Dex, Keefe, or Fitz, as well as the magnificent writing talent Mrs. Messenger has for this series, I would definitely turn this series over. I can only hope and pray that Flashback will be better and can actually PROGRESS further into the series. <br><br>*mic drop*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531061071ra/25941875.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1862055704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1862055704" />
    <a title="Mariam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31657573-mariam"><img alt="Mariam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601068489p2/31657573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1862055704?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariam" href="/user/show/31657573-mariam">Mariam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481497404" href="/book/show/34228217-nightfall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=2017-publication">2017-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=best-cast">best-cast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1862055704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16775777028601487292"><blockquote>
  <i>Can we stop pretending this is a dinner party and get back to why you have a drawing of the Nightfall symbol?</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Please do.<br/><br/>WARNING: RANT AHEAD<br/><br/>So many characters and alter-egos and talking and the love triangle/square that ultimately makes me hate Keefe (I'm sorry! I don't want to!) and all of this <i>chaos.</i> There's only so much you can put in a series, Shannon Messenger. I'm sorry, but this is too much.<br/><br/>A List of My Issues:<br/><br/>1. Too Many Characters<br/><br/>I miss the old crew. They were well-defined characters </span>
  <span id="freeText16775777028601487292" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Can we stop pretending this is a dinner party and get back to why you have a drawing of the Nightfall symbol?</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Please do.<br /><br />WARNING: RANT AHEAD<br /><br />So many characters and alter-egos and talking and the love triangle/square that ultimately makes me hate Keefe (I'm sorry! I don't want to!) and all of this <i>chaos.</i> There's only so much you can put in a series, Shannon Messenger. I'm sorry, but this is too much.<br /><br />A List of My Issues:<br /><br />1. Too Many Characters<br /><br />I miss the old crew. They were well-defined characters that I treasured. But now? They hardly show up in the book! Dex is shoved into the background where he makes random gadgets appear to advance the plot, Fitz has officially earned the title of "Sophie's Energy Booster" and nothing more (MY POOR BABY WHY.) The two newer characters, Linh and Tam, aren't too bad, but the bodyguards and Black Swan members keep throwing me off because there are so many of them! <s>That may be my fault, though, because I didn't get the chance to reread the previous book before reading this book.</s><br /><br />2. No One Knows What the Hell is Going On<br /><br /><i>“I know you’re still refusing to see me as anything more than a villain in this conflict, but like it or not, I’m the only one trying to build a solution.” <br />“To what?” Sophie asked. <br />“Problems you’re still not ready to face.</i><br /><br />That's code for "IDK." Please remind me what the bad guys are being bad for because I honestly don't remember. And it doesn't seem anyone in the book remembers either.<br /><br />3. The WORST Love Triangle/Square I Have Ever Faced<br /><br /><i>Twilight's</i> love triangle was bad. <i>Red Queen's</i> love triangle was bad. Heck, <i>The Hunger Games'</i> love triangle was bad because ALL love triangles are bad. But what makes <i>Nightfall's</i> love triangle/square/thing the worst?<br /><br />I love Keefe, Fitz, and Dex. Since book one, I have learned to love them, and when it comes to choosing one of them for Sophie, it's only natural I have to cringe when the other two have a "moment" with her. Dex didn't suffer too badly, but poor, poor Keefe did. <i>Every time</i> he even gets close to Sophie I find myself hating him which makes me want to cry. <br /><br />4. The Plot<br /><br />The series is going in circles. Repetition, repetition, repetition. Enough said. Specifically, though, <i>Nightfall's</i> plot was atrociously weak. There was a whole lot of sitting around a table and planning, and very little doing. And the lack of explanation really turned me off.<br /><br />5. Fitz<br /><br />Fitz has been my favorite character since book one so he deserves a category of his own. Not once in the entire book did he get to show off <i>his</i> skills and much of his personality was smothered by Sophie and Keefe. He is a delicate character, a character that I tucked under my wing and watched blossom from "Wonderboy" to a man that will stop at nothing to protect his friends. He deserves so much better and I adored every moment he made an appearance in <i>Nightfall</i>. <s>Seriously, though, he's gotten so touchy-feely with Sophie. He's wearing <i>cologne</i> now. My little cinnamon roll is all grown up.</s><br /><br /><i>“Tell me about it,” Fitz said, fanning the front of his red bramble jersey. “I was halfway through my morning run when Blur showed up—so now I’m all sweaty.” <br />“And smelling awesome,” Keefe added with a choked cough.</i><br /><br />God, I miss the Fitz/Keefe friendship. And the Sophie/Biana friendship.<br /><br />But most of all, I miss the old, simplistic plot. I love Shannon Messenger's writing, I really do, but not this book. Try again next time?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16775777028601487292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2176578327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176578327" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7746586-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339550875p2/7746586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176578327?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/7746586-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34884513-nightfall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176578327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16957878403101783576"><strong>This book disappointed me...</strong><br/><br/>I wanted to love this book. I really did. I have been a fan of this series since the beginning...BEFORE it became popular. But sadly, this book fell flat.<br/><br/>You know those books that you read and by the end you are like, meh, what just happened? Or that book that is the second book in a trilogy, where nothing actually happens thus or becomes a 'filler' book.<br/><br/>Sadly, that was this book. Nothing really happen. It was pages upon pages of nothing . So now I am going to list al</span>
  <span id="freeText16957878403101783576" style="display:none"><strong>This book disappointed me...</strong><br /><br />I wanted to love this book. I really did. I have been a fan of this series since the beginning...BEFORE it became popular. But sadly, this book fell flat.<br /><br />You know those books that you read and by the end you are like, meh, what just happened? Or that book that is the second book in a trilogy, where nothing actually happens thus or becomes a 'filler' book.<br /><br />Sadly, that was this book. Nothing really happen. It was pages upon pages of nothing . So now I am going to list all the things I feel went wrong with the book.<br /><br />1. Sophie<br />I honestly don't even know how to begin with her. Here we are at book 6 and Sophie is STILL the little helpless weakling we met in book 1. We spend almost the entire book in Sophie's head. And all we read about is her anxiety and worries about everything that is going on. This is suppose to be our heroine and yet she needs EVERYONE to save her. They keep important information from her because she is too delicate to handle it. What drove me the craziest was that it was never ending. Around and around and around she went, worry worry worry. On top of all of that, she barely even used any of her awesome powers. I was also annoyed that she constantly asked her friends if they were sure they wanted to help. Again, this is BOOK SIX. They have been helping since book ONE. Of COURSE they will say yes! On top of that, this is not just Sophie's battle. It affects all of them but she acts like it is only her that is affects. I was just so disappointed in this character.<br /><br />2. No character development <br />No one progressed or grew in this story. Well, maybe Keefe did a little bit by the end of the book but no one else did. Really, all the characters felt quite flat. But then that might be due to the fact that NOTHING HAPPENED until the very end of the story.<br /><br />3. Love triangle<br />I am so over this. Just pick one already. Or pick none. At this point, I honestly don't even care anymore. Just please stop shoving it down our throats.<br /><br />4. NOTHING HAPPENS<br />The entire book, we see our characters mainly just trying to figure what the Neverseen is up to. They are researching and generally just trying to disiphor clues. And of course we have weak old Sophie who pulls her eyelashes out and panics over every single little thing. Now don't get me wrong. The book answers some questions that we've had and there are a few surprises along the way. But it's just not enough. Way too much time was spend on basically nothing. Things really didn't start picking up until the end of the story. Things happened (I won't spoil it) and then we re left with yet another cliffhanger. <br /><br />5. Amy/ Sophie's parents<br />After that cliffhanger of an ending from book 5, I really thought we would see more of them or read more about them. But nope. Again, I won't give any spoilers but I was just highly disappointed in this. <br /> <br />Honestly, as much as I love this series, I wish she would have stopped this at 5 books. Now it just seems like she is stretching it to make more money. But it's not working. Thankfully, the next book will be the last. Of course I will read it since I have inserted so much time in this story and I want to know how it ends. I can only hope that it has the epic ending it deserves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16957878403101783576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2260299272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2256325812630341704">I almost didn't write this review. I've thought about it a lot over the past couple of weeks... Basically the lack of caps and adding in a bunch of extra voooooooowels makes me wonder if it's worth my time. You see where I'm going with this? Read the top like 3 pages of reviews and you'll get it.<br/><br/>In short, I'm a bit snarky on the subject. I am, really. I know it. Why? Because this book, this series, is really really good. There's a lot of things amazing about it and it's a lot deeper than you'd g</span>
  <span id="freeText2256325812630341704" style="display:none">I almost didn't write this review. I've thought about it a lot over the past couple of weeks... Basically the lack of caps and adding in a bunch of extra voooooooowels makes me wonder if it's worth my time. You see where I'm going with this? Read the top like 3 pages of reviews and you'll get it.<br /><br />In short, I'm a bit snarky on the subject. I am, really. I know it. Why? Because this book, this series, is really really good. There's a lot of things amazing about it and it's a lot deeper than you'd guess. AND PEOPLE MISS IT. Oh hey, caps. <br /><br />Why do people miss it? Because of something extremely stupid. It's called a love triangle. I'm not sure how far Shannon had originally met to take that but I'm sure at one point she was smart enough to realize that about 99% of her readership only cared about THAT. Now... you can call it a smart business move(it is) or you can call it a crutch(I am). It's smart because it really doesn't matter how good or bad these books are, the main readership only cares to plow through it and lap up the love triangle bits. (Don't worry about my safety. The lack of fangirling and squealing will bury this review and no one will ever know.)<br /><br />It's a crutch because where this story COULD be leaning on the AMAZING description, plot, details, character development, and deeper messages, it instead makes sure the love triangle is every present and frequent enough where even if you want to forget it(I do), you can't. <br /><br />Shannon... You. Don't. Need. This. You're a better author than this and your books are better than this. I know, I know, we're six in and it's too late and $$$. <br /><br />Honestly, the love triangle is the one thing killing this series for me. I hate love triangles and unlike everyone else that picks their favorite and hope he wins the magic prize called *girl*. I hope the best doesn't get her because he darn well deserves better. Which making me dislike your MC is probably never the author intention, but there it is.<br /><br />Basically, I wish I could read reviews about what people actually thought of the book. Not ones that are pre-publishing squealing, and post-reading squealing about who they want to win the girl. And with the decided lack, it really kills my motivation to want to write a review. I am, but is this a review? No. Not really. It doesn't talk about what I like or dislike. Let's face it, this is a big book. There's a lot of content to discuss. Heck, even some discussion on the romance angles would be nice but it just makes me ill because thank you I've had too much of THAT.<br /><br />*grumble grumble* goes the old lady. And in summary, this is another great book in the series with a plot that forces you to keep reading, interesting characters, and those secret deeper moments that have really sold me on this series. There's also the annoying love triangle that will be dragged out for the entire series and I try to ignore it, but it does at least taint my love of KotLC. <br /><br />Recommended for people who might actually want some decent content, people who are only here for more KEEFEFITZ baloney, and lovers of love triangles. (but seriously, if you haven't read this series you should and just ignore the lurveeee and enjoy the actual content. It's darn good.<br /><br />Now to hide from the mob. Bwahahaha.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2256325812630341704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3566746656" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3566746656" />
    <a title="Nikki " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/113608617-nikki"><img alt="Nikki " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604074340p2/113608617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3566746656?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki " href="/user/show/113608617-nikki">Nikki </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3566746656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3527339908455742481">GUYS PLEASE READ THIS IT TOOK ME FOREVER TO WRITE: <br/><br/>This book was tough. Scary. Beyond sad and sorrowful. Idk how they deemed this as a middle grade, it's a solid YA in my book.<br/><br/>First off, I think this was the strongest book for a lot of the characters. I got such warm feelings from a lot of scenes, and I really felt like I was in-person with these characters, because I know them so damn well. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I don't ship Sodex, but I think the kiss really added a lot to this narrative. Shannon Me</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3527339908455742481" style="display:none">GUYS PLEASE READ THIS IT TOOK ME FOREVER TO WRITE: <br /><br />This book was tough. Scary. Beyond sad and sorrowful. Idk how they deemed this as a middle grade, it's a solid YA in my book.<br /><br />First off, I think this was the strongest book for a lot of the characters. I got such warm feelings from a lot of scenes, and I really felt like I was in-person with these characters, because I know them so damn well. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I don't ship Sodex, but I think the kiss really added a lot to this narrative. Shannon Messenger put it in at a really valuable time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, we get a lot of Bronte, especially in the second half of the book. I really love him in the books (yes he's thousands of years old, I know) but I love how the crew got to make a little more peace with him. Also, I loved Keefe more than ever in this book. He's really been growing into a funny, kind, risk-it-all person. This was such a character-centric book, and I love that. <br /><br />This is the first book where we really take a deep trip into the black hole that is Sophie's mental health. She's struggling a lot with many things, especially the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ kidnapping of her parents  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It was scary and incredibly sad to think that this is how Sophie's been feeling the past books. She was MADE for being an incredible person, and with that much pressure on her, it's hard for her to cope. I just want to see a book where all she does is go out to movies with her friends and plays in the garden. LIKE THAT'S ALL. STOP PUTTING SO MUCH PRESSURE ON MY BABY. <br /><br />The reason her mental health was so powerful was because: the whole time in this book, it felt like we where reading through Sophie's foggy but somehow clear vision. We saw everything THROUGH her, therefore embodying her struggles.<br /><br />And I think that's one of the reasons why many people started not liking the series after this book. This didn't have much of a stable plot, only a few solid plot points that will probably fall into place later in the series. It was probably 75% character growth and 25% plot. I think both focuses (plot and character) work for different installments of the series.<br /><br />Also, I used to not really like Tam. Frankly, I'm a bit embarrassed about that. He is amazing- omg?!? He is GOD TIER if I ever tier rank the characters. I also really like our new character, Ro, Keefe's bodyguard. <br /><br />Side Note About Romance: <br /><br />Fitz is a cheap piece of crap that Sophie doesn't deserve. How does he try to win Sophie's love? By bringing her GIFTS?!? He makes her bracelets and gives her homemade desserts. Have you seen anything cheaper than that?? I understand, that would be considered a romantic gesture among other things, but that's all he does. And he always wants to be with her, and he brings up the excuse: "bUt wE aRe CoGnAtEs!" Save the shit for someone else, Sophie is a strong woman who doesn't need you.<br /><br />Keefe, on the other hand, has risked his life repeatedly for the well-being of Sophie. Yes, he's done some pretty bad things that's put Sophie into a state of depression, but he is loyal time after time again. All his life, all his choices, are based on "How will this effect Sophie?" Honestly, he needs to put that energy into self-love, because he thinks he is trash when he is obviously not... :( <br /><br />As for Dex, there's a special love between him and Sophie that can't be erased. They love each other, but they aren't IN love. They've went through so much stuff together, and popularity and cliques within the 10 or so main teen characters have made him less of a priority. I hate that. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the kidnapping in the first book, for example! They both deeply care for each other and will always be in each other's lives no matter what, it's just platonic.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />IN CONCLUSION: <br /><br />This is quite a long review, but I definitely loved this book. The books are dragging a bit. However, I'm always going to be here for the Keeper crew :) <br /><br />If I haven't already made it clear, you need to read this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3527339908455742481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14326018977575903880">1. PLOT<br/>Repetition, repetition and more repetition. <br/>At this point in time, the series is merely going round and round in circles. The plot was unnecessarily long and filled with rather mundane details at times. Nightfall is one of the weakest books, plot-wise, in the entire series. <br/><br/>2. SOPHIE AND CO<br/>I love the dynamics of the group, and their banter - but the group has become rather large: Dex was practically shoved to the background, Fitz became Sophie’s official mind booster... Tam and Linh were </span>
  <span id="freeText14326018977575903880" style="display:none">1. PLOT<br />Repetition, repetition and more repetition. <br />At this point in time, the series is merely going round and round in circles. The plot was unnecessarily long and filled with rather mundane details at times. Nightfall is one of the weakest books, plot-wise, in the entire series. <br /><br />2. SOPHIE AND CO<br />I love the dynamics of the group, and their banter - but the group has become rather large: Dex was practically shoved to the background, Fitz became Sophie’s official mind booster... Tam and Linh were alright, but it felt like their presence was unnecessary, at times. <br /><br />3. LOVE TRIANGLES<br />Sophie, Fitz and Keefe. Ugh. Love triangles are bad in general, and in this case, rather unnecessary. <br /><br />4. ONE-DIMENSIONAL VILLAINS<br />Lady Gisela seemed to be the “villain” just for the sake of being one - Vespera and Fintan too. The series is the classic Good VS Evil, with evil having no reason to be there but to move the plot along.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2970864426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2970864426" />
    <a title="BrooKe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke"><img alt="BrooKe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583732525p2/87485390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2970864426?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrooKe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrooKe" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke">BrooKe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2970864426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2332330376851458343">4.6/5 | I think—I <i>
  <b>think</b>
</i>—I may have been blinded by sheer entertainment value so maybe, just <i>maybe</i>, this really shouldn’t get 5 stars and I’m a liiiiiiiiittle bit biased.<br/><br/>I believe it is high time I addressed the key question of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_' title='Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Keeper of the Lost Cities</a> series: <b>Do I think someone tugging their eyelashes out when they’re nervous is a thing?</b><br/><br/>My answer: <br/><b>Yes, yes I do.</b> As a matter of fact, I had the exact same habit when I was ten up until I was thirteen or fourteen. It’s a thing, guys. It may</span>
  <span id="freeText2332330376851458343" style="display:none">4.6/5 | I think—I <i>
  <b>think</b>
</i>—I may have been blinded by sheer entertainment value so maybe, just <i>maybe</i>, this really shouldn’t get 5 stars and I’m a liiiiiiiiittle bit biased.<br /><br />I believe it is high time I addressed the key question of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a> series: <b>Do I think someone tugging their eyelashes out when they’re nervous is a thing?</b><br /><br />My answer: <br /><b>Yes, yes I do.</b> As a matter of fact, I had the exact same habit when I was ten up until I was thirteen or fourteen. It’s a thing, guys. It may sound creepy but it’s just like biting your nails (only, granted, slightly more damaging to your appearance).<br /><br /><br /><b>P L O T</b><br /><br /><i>Blah.</i><br /><br />What even was the plot? <br /><br />I’ll start with the good: the morals. (Okay, maybe that isn’t strictly plot but it kind of fits into this section more than any other so let’s roll with it.)<br /><br />The morals this story promotes are so healthy for the human mind. When this series doesn’t drop bombshells that fuck with my brain, I actually feel like a better person after reading them. It’s just so wholesome.<br /><br />This instalment also brought the best action sequences <i>by far</i> in the series. The Nightfall and Atlantis battles had such verbal and physical conflict that had me soaring through this book (like a moonlark (<b>hehe</b>). It’s what drove me to make the somewhat impulsive decision of hitting that 5 star rating! And I don’t even regret it.<br /><br />On the topic of the moonlark, I acknowledge I wasn’t big on the whole ‘Chosen One’ trope initially, but... The metaphor is so beautiful!!! In the first three or so books, having everything centred around Sophie elicited <b>MAJOR</b> eye-rolls from me practically every chapter. Since then, it’s been somewhat remedied. For example, by giving Keefe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a legacy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, he is thus more crucial to the plot, widening its horizons. I only wish more would be done with the other 46281 characters!<br /><br />I liked how the plot capitalised more on the flaws of the elves, addressing namely their vanity and their mental fragility. Also, I hadn’t even considered divorce being a thing in the Lost Cities! My jaw <i>hit the floor</i> when it was first so casually represented!<br /><br />My main and only <i>real</i> issue was the ‘plot twist’ that happened around 200-ish (total guesstimate) pages in? Plot twist? <b>Try plot convenience</b>! It seemed like it was just randomly thrown in there because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger" title="Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Messenger</a> realised she’d made things a whole lot harder for her future-self at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>! Just because the characters experience mind-fucks doesn’t mean it’s okay to do that to the readers!<br /><br />Also, I think I’m starting to sense a pattern with the Keeper books. This one’s plot seemed awfully similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260670.Exile__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___2_" title="Exile (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #2) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Exile</a> and Lodestar... I wouldn’t classify the repetition as tiresome <i>just yet</i> but I really do hope it dulls in the coming books.<br /><br />Totally random thought:<br />You know what would be really interesting? <b>Getting a look into the Della-Alden-Alina love triangle</b>! That must have been simultaneously hilarious and <i>suuuper</i> dramatic! Even if it were delivered by means of simple exposition, I require more details!<br /><br /><br /><b>C H A R A C T E R S</b><br /><br /><i>“Dex was already waiting for her when she made her way downstairs. So was Bronte. And Mr. Forkle. And Alden and Della. And Grady and Edaline. And Tam, Linh, Biana, Fitz, Keefe, Grizel, Woltzer, Lovise and Ro.”</i><br /><br />It’s paragraphs like this that make me wonder if perhaps there might be too many characters...<br /><br />Like, why introduce Vespera when you already have Fintan, Ruy, Gethen, Brant AND Gisela? And all of these guys are supposed to have their own unique vendetta? Ruy, Gethen and Fintan could easily be condensed into one character, leaving Gisela and Brant who are interesting, sure, but one of which <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[was killed off like <b>POOF!</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the other of which is inconsistent <i>as fuck</i>. I really hope no new characters that are meant to be significant enter the picture because, with each new entry, <b>the current cast suffers</b>.<br /><br />Sophie, my innocent, precious baby. As much as I love her, her character is beginning to seem a little... <i>stagnant</i>. What I mean is, for a protagonist who goes through so many hardships, you’d think she’d show a little more growth? The lack of this quality became very apparent to me due to the sheer amount of parallels drawn between this book and Book 1, what with the inclusion of Sophie’s human family.<br /><br />And if Sophie’s human family is the theme here, I’ll confess that it only took two chapters for me to like Amy more than I liked Sophie after the first entire book! I’ll just... take that as a sign of improved writing.<br /><br />I remember in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a> review when I raved about how Keefe never failed to make me smile. Half the time, he still does, but, during the other half, he genuinely makes me cry. <b>And I am totally okay with that</b>. <br /><br />My strong respect for Keefe continues to grow after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_" title="Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfall</a>. He’s irrational and reckless but he’s so clever, easily the bravest and <b>selfless to a fault</b>. He’s so deeply flawed that I cannot help but adore him and just when I think I’ve figured him out, he shows a new side to him. See, that’s the thing! <b>There is always so much more to him!</b><br /><br /><i>“Ah. The Vacker boy is around,” Lady Gisela said. “And still contributing very little it seems.”</i><br /><br />Hey, I didn’t say anything! Gisela said it!<br /><br /><br />...but, like, I meannnnnnn...... <i>she lowkey right</i>.<br /><br />Honestly, I don't think I can blame Fitz for being so bland. If anything, his character is facing injustice. <b>I think he’s just a casualty of too many characters being included and not enough of them being developed properly</b>. But seeing as he’s on a good 40-ish% of the established covers, he really should be more of a priority.<br /><br />Biana is such a legend. If she wants something, she sure as hell will go after it! For example, when she outright told Tam to take his shirt off, covering it up with innocent logic. And when she rugby tackled the villains that scared the crap out of everyone else? Awesome. <b>I aspire to be like Biana.</b> Plus, she has <i>remarkable</i> taste in guys: Keefe, and now Tam.<br /><br />I love Tam. He’s such an angsty guy and I love me some angst. He is consistently entertaining and engaging and is a true asset to the books. Linh’s character arc made me emotional; The Girl of Many Floods came full circle! I’m so glad that monumental moment was captured <b>so <i>perfectly</i></b> on the cover. <br /><br />Marella was kind of pointless. Then again, half of the characters were. On a positive note: Ro is most definitely a strong addition! <br /><br />And, look, <b>just because Dex and Sophie ain’t gonna happen doesn’t mean Dex don’t gotta happen at all</b>! Like, where the hell was he the entire book?<br /><br /><i>“But then the voice added, “There’s no reason to worry,” and she rushed back to consciousness in a wave of fury. <br />She only knew one person who used that expression.”</i><br /><br />You mean she only knew <b>one</b> person who used that expression 45 times! That is <b>golden</b> characterisation right there. God, I love Alden.<br /><br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>I would like to take this moment to commemorate the passing of a ship. SophiexDex, while you never stood out to me, I honour thy sacrifice. May you rest in peace. </i><br /><br />Although, if Sophie and Dex don’t remain best friends till the end, so help me, I will rampage!!! Now, if only a certain <i>other ship could kindly bugger off so my precious Sokeefe would finally set sail!</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(If you consider that a spoiler because you have yet to read any of the instalments to the Keeper of the Lost Cities series, I ask you this: Wtf are you doing here reading a review of Book 6?! Never fear; I have recently found a handy dandy lil' format here that will hopefully block out spoiler-y sentences!)<br /><br /><b>This perfectly encapsulates my ship:</b><br /><i>“...fists curled with fury, eyes watery, skin pale from shock, hands shaking with a nervous, almost hopeful energy. But when it was his turn to speak, he chose to move to where Sophie sat curled in one of the armchairs and crouched down to her eye level to ask how </i>she<i> was doing.”</i><br /><br />Sophie and Keefe are so fluffy. They’re kittens. They’re actually fluffy, little kittens. And I’m the mother cat, calling to them in the form of crying to come to me and be united.<br /><br /><i>“But on the sixth step, her ankle wobbled, and she would’ve toppled to the left if Keefe hadn’t been ready to nudge her back to the right.<br />“Not a word,” she told him, realising his prediction about when she’d trip had come true.”</i><br /><br />Okay, so <i>lemme get this straight</i>. Not only did Keefe correctly predict exactly when Sophie would fall, he also came up to Sophie’s right, as if he knew she would fall in that direction. Dude has a sixth sense for her. On the <b>SIXTH</b> step! <i>Ahaha, I’m <b>so clever</b>.</i><br /><br /><b>[For coherent Sokeefe analysis, please visit my previous reviews of [book:Exile|13260670], <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260668.Everblaze__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___3_" title="Everblaze (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #3) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Everblaze</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22733616.Neverseen__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___4_" title="Neverseen (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #4) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverseen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272698.Lodestar__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___5_" title="Lodestar (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #5) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Lodestar</a>.]</b><br /><br /><i>“I never thought I’d need a stuffed animal to sleep. But... I never knew I needed a lot of things before I met you.”</i><br />Ahhh. The Keefoster feels get me every tiiiime.<br /><br />Just when I’m all set to completely dismiss Fitz and Sophie, they have to go and have a genuinely sweet moment! <b>AGH!</b> Damn you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger" title="Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Messenger</a>! Why can't you make this easy for me?! <i>(Not that there’s a doubt in my mind that this won’t ever live up to Sophie and Keefe. Just because I don’t think this is better doesn’t mean I don’t like it at all.)</i><br /><br />See, Sophie and Fitz are starting to get all romance-y, and it’s so CORNY! That makes it simultaneously adorable and the slightest bit gag-worthy.<br /><br /><i>“The funny thing was, neither of them realised how much they had in common. If they’d get over themselves, they’d probably be best friends.”</i><br /><br />Can this happen already? Tam and Keefe would be the <i>ultimate</i> dream team. Their constant sniping at each other will have to quell my needs for now.<br /><br />Similarly, Fitz, Keefe: <i>Are you boys familiar with the saying ‘bros before hoes’?</i> Even if Sophie is a <b>far</b> cry from that, how am I supposed to believe these two are still best friends? Like... <i>really</i>? As much as I’m rooting for Sokeefe, I don’t think it’s super cool of Keefe to be so close to Sophie in that way when he knows, more than anyone, how much Sophie and Fitz like each other in that way. Then again, maybe he’d be more cautious if Fitz spoke two words to him.<br /><br />... ...<br /><br />In terms of shipping, I know what’s coming next... and I’m not ready. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2332330376851458343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3q1GUiI+YlGlpPgr+g4V0ddNdWa6Gv2VxJz5Qxt+DR4woT9pFyYU1mdxUWMswYWPNqleeFbTgM/EygEw06fDBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gOi8rjjfhLc7dp3tqg1Tz949vnY4ecF3N9xd8aEDDsRu5MWVDcfyMPmjNKV8wsORP9mVaNSwvC03iqWCadrA3w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
